<li id="cite_note-frana-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-frana_100-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFFrances2013"><a href="/wiki/Allen_Frances" title="Allen Frances">Frances A</a> (August 2013). <a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.7326%2F0003-4819-159-3-201308060-00655" rel="nofollow">"The new crisis of confidence in psychiatric diagnosis"</a>. Ideas and Opinions. <i>Annals of Internal Medicine</i>. <b>159</b> (3): 221–2. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.7326%2F0003-4819-159-3-201308060-00655" rel="nofollow">10.7326/0003-4819-159-3-201308060-00655</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/23685989" rel="nofollow">23685989</a>. <q>Unfortunately, the extensive research has had no effect on psychiatric diagnosis, which still relies exclusively on fallible subjective judgments rather than objective biological tests. … In the past 20 years, the rate of attention-deficit disorder tripled, the rate of bipolar disorder doubled, and the rate of autism increased more than 20-fold (4). The lesson should be clear that every change in the diagnostic system can lead to unpredictable overdiagnosis.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Annals+of+Internal+Medicine&amp;rft.atitle=The+new+crisis+of+confidence+in+psychiatric+diagnosis&amp;rft.volume=159&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=221-2&amp;rft.date=2013-08&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.7326%2F0003-4819-159-3-201308060-00655&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F23685989&amp;rft.aulast=Frances&amp;rft.aufirst=A&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fdoi.org%2F10.7326%252F0003-4819-159-3-201308060-00655&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMental+disorder"></span></span>

(identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/35502519" rel="nofollow">35502519</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:248503963" rel="nofollow">248503963</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Psychiatric+Services&amp;rft.atitle=Downward+National+Trends+in+Mental+Health+Treatment+Offered+in+Spanish%3A+State+Differences+by+Proportion+of+Hispanic+Residents&amp;rft.pages=appi.ps.202100614&amp;rft.date=2022-05-03&amp;rft.issn=1075-2730&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A248503963%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F35502519&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1176%2Fappi.ps.202100614&amp;rft.aulast=Pro&amp;rft.aufirst=George&amp;rft.au=Brown%2C+Clare&amp;rft.au=Rojo%2C+Martha&amp;rft.au=Patel%2C+Jenil&amp;rft.au=Flax%2C+Chasmine&amp;rft.au=Haynes%2C+Tiffany&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fps.psychiatryonline.org%2Fdoi%2F10.1176%2Fappi.ps.202100614&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMental+disorder"></span> "Disparities in behavioral health risk factors in the past decade have also grown and closely parallel the overall growth in the Latin American population (11–13). From 2015 to 2018, rates of serious mental illness in Latin American populations increased by 60% (from 4.0% to 6.4%) among those ages 18–25 years and by 77% (from 2.2% to 3.9%) among those ages 26–49 years (14). This report was based on analysis of the National Survey on Drug Use and Health and used the Substance Abuse and Mental Health Services Administration’s (SAMHSA’s) definition of serious mental illness as a diagnosable mental, behavior, or emotional disorder that causes serious functional impairment that substantially interferes with one or more major life activities (15). A similar trend between 2015 and 2018 has been observed for the prevalence of major depressive episodes among Latin Americans ages 12–49 years, which increased from 8.4% to 11.3% (14). In a study based on data from the Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System, more than one-third (34%) of Latin American respondents reported at least one poor mental health day in the past month (mean=3.6 days), and 11% reported frequent mental distress (16)."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://minorityhealth.hhs.gov/omh/browse.aspx?lvl=4&amp;lvlid=69" rel="nofollow">"Mental and Behavioral Health - Hispanics - The Office of Minority Health"</a>. <i>minorityhealth.hhs.gov</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=minorityhealth.hhs.gov&amp;rft.atitle=Mental+and+Behavioral+Health+-+Hispanics+-+The+Office+of+Minority+Health&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fminorityhealth.hhs.gov%2Fomh%2Fbrowse.aspx%3Flvl%3D4%26lvlid%3D69&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMental+disorder"></span> "However, the suicide rate for [Latin Americans] is less than half that of the non-[Latin American] white population.
In 2019, suicide was the second leading cause of death for Latin Americans, ages 15 to 34.1"</span>
</li>
